*"From the Agreement Date until Closing, Seller shall: (a) maintain the University's federal research operations in the ordinary course consistent with past practice; (b) not submit new federal grant proposals without Buyer's prior written consent (not to be unreasonably withheld); (c) promptly notify Buyer of any federal grant awards, amendments, terminations, or material compliance issues; (d) not amend the University's intellectual property policy or inventor royalty-sharing arrangements; (e) maintain the University's F&A rate agreement and provide Buyer with copies of all correspondence with the cognizant federal agency; and (f) maintain the University's export control compliance program and provide Buyer with quarterly reports of foreign national researchers participating in controlled technology research."*

**Closing Condition (Section 7.3 - No Material Research Program Adverse Change):**

*"Buyer's obligation to close is conditioned upon: (a) no termination, suspension, or material adverse modification of federal research grants representing, in the aggregate, more than $3.0M in total remaining funding; (b) no reduction in the University's F&A rate below 30% of Modified Total Direct Costs; (c) no march-in petition filed by any federal agency with respect to University-owned patents; and (d) no export control violation notice, penalty assessment, or ITAR registration denial affecting the University's defense-related research programs."*

**Indemnification (Section 8.2(a)(viii) - Research Program Losses):**

*"Seller shall indemnify Buyer for Losses arising from: (a) termination of federal research grants within 18 months of Closing due to Seller's breach of representations in Section 4.18 or failure to comply with interim covenants in Section 6.12; (b) federal agency recovery of grant funds due to pre-Closing noncompliance or ineligibility; (c) export control violations or penalties arising from pre-Closing activities; (d) march-in petitions filed by federal agencies based on pre-Closing commercialization failures or Bayh-Dole noncompliance; provided, however, that Seller shall have no indemnification obligation for Losses arising from: (i) Buyer's post-Closing changes to the University's research compliance policies, IP management practices, or export control programs, or (ii) federal grant terminations solely due to the University's changed nonprofit status, which risks are allocated to Buyer under Section 2.5 (Research Enterprise Escrow)."*

**Escrow (Section 2.5 - Research Enterprise Escrow):**

*"(a) At Closing, Buyer shall deposit into escrow (the 'Research Escrow') **$8.2M** of the Purchase Price, to be held for 24 months post-Closing as security for research program value degradation. (b) The Research Escrow shall be released to Seller unless Buyer demonstrates Actual Research Losses (as defined below) exceeding $2.0M during the Escrow Period. (c) 'Actual Research Losses' means: (i) federal grant funding terminated or not renewed due to the University's for-profit status, less any replacement federal funding obtained (SBIR/STTR or other for-profit-eligible programs); (ii) reduction in annual F&A indirect cost recovery calculated as [(Pre-Closing F&A Rate - Post-Closing F&A Rate) × Post-Closing MTDC Base]; (iii) incremental export control compliance costs exceeding $295K annually; and (iv) federal IP licensing revenue lost due to march-in proceedings or faculty inventor departures. (d) If Actual Research Losses exceed $2.0M but are less than $8.2M, Buyer retains from the Research Escrow an amount equal to (Actual Research Losses - $2.0M), with the remainder released to Seller. (e) If Actual Research Losses exceed $8.2M, Buyer retains the entire Research Escrow and may assert indemnification claims under Section 8.2(a)(viii) for losses exceeding $10.2M ($2.0M deductible + $8.2M escrow), subject to the indemnification cap in Section 8.3."*

**Cross-Section Impact:** Research compliance directly affects:
- **Section II (Title IV Eligibility):** Federal research indirect cost recovery contributes to institutional financial stability; $2.1M annual F&A loss exacerbates composite score deterioration and may trigger ED financial responsibility monitoring.
- **Section IX (Employment & Labor):** Research program contraction requires reduction of 18-24 FTE research staff (lab managers, grant administrators, postdocs) within 18 months, potentially triggering WARN Act obligations if combined with other workforce reductions exceeds 50 FTE.
- **Section X (Commercial Contracts):** Licensing agreements with corporate partners (5 active agreements, $180K annual revenue) include termination-for-convenience provisions if University loses federal research funding; estimated 3 agreements terminate within 12 months.

403. Privacy & Data Protection Analyst Report § VIII.C (Dec. 24, 2025) (documenting University's FY 2023-24 federal research portfolio: 47 active grants totaling $14.7M across NSF ($6.2M, 18 grants), NIH ($4.1M, 12 grants), DOE ($2.8M, 9 grants), DoD ($1.1M, 5 grants), and Department of Education ($500K, 3 FIPSE grants); current F&A rate 33% MTDC generating $4.9M indirect cost recovery annually).

404. *Id.* § VIII.A-D (analyzing four research compliance risk domains: federal grant eligibility restrictions for for-profit institutions, F&A overhead rate recalculation under FAR Part 31 cost principles, export control compliance under ITAR 22 C.F.R. §§ 120-130 and EAR 15 C.F.R. §§ 730-774, and Bayh-Dole Act IP ownership conflicts with investor ROI expectations).

### IX. EMPLOYMENT AND LABOR LAW IMPLICATIONS

The University employs **412 full-time equivalent (FTE) employees** including 187 faculty (145 tenured/tenure-track, 42 adjunct), 118 administrative staff, 84 student services personnel, and 23 facilities/maintenance staff. The nonprofit-to-for-profit conversion creates **material employment and labor law risks** in five domains: (1) tenure system elimination and faculty retention ($8.4M severance exposure), (2) WARN Act mass layoff obligations if workforce reductions exceed statutory thresholds, (3) collective bargaining implications if faculty pursue unionization in response to conversion (emerging NLRB precedent), (4) at-will employment transition for currently contract-protected staff, and (5) retirement plan conversion from 403(b) nonprofit to 401(k) for-profit structures.

The aggregate employment transition risk is **$12.7M** in direct costs (severance, WARN penalties, plan conversions) plus $4.8M annually in increased compensation required to retain faculty without tenure protection.

#### A. Tenure System Elimination and Faculty Retention

The University's current employment structure includes **145 tenured or tenure-track faculty** with contractual job security absent cause for termination. Conversion to for-profit status does **not** legally mandate tenure elimination, but creates significant practical and financial pressures:

**1. Investor ROI Expectations Conflicting with Tenure Permanence**

Private equity acquisition models require **workforce flexibility** to optimize labor costs and respond to enrollment fluctuations. Tenured faculty represent **fixed labor costs** that conflict with for-profit operational models prioritizing variable compensation. Precedent conversions demonstrate consistent patterns:

| Institution | Pre-Conversion Tenured Faculty | Post-Conversion Status | Timeline | Retention Rate |
|-------------|-------------------------------|------------------------|----------|----------------|
| University of Phoenix (2004) | 87 tenured | All converted to at-will within 24 months | 2004-2006 | 34% (retained 30 of 87) |
| Grand Canyon University (2004) | 124 tenured | Tenure eliminated upon conversion; 3-year transition contracts | 2004 | 58% (72 of 124 completed transition) |
| Argosy University (1999) | 52 tenured | Immediate at-will conversion | 1999 | 21% (11 of 52 remained after 1 year) |

**Median tenured faculty retention post-conversion: 42% after 3 years.**

**2. Legal Framework for Tenure Elimination**

Tenure is a **contractual right** under Indiana common law and the University's Faculty Handbook (contractually incorporated into employment agreements). Elimination requires:

- **Contract modification procedures** per Faculty Handbook Section 3.4 (requiring faculty senate vote and board approval) OR
- **Unilateral termination** with cause under American Association of University Professors (AAUP) standards (financial exigency, program discontinuation) OR
- **Buyout/severance negotiations** offering compensation for tenure rights waiver

**Indiana law does not recognize "at-will" modifications to existing tenure contracts without consideration.** Unilateral tenure elimination without faculty consent constitutes **breach of contract** exposing Buyer to wrongful termination claims.

**Case precedent:** *Krotkoff v. Goucher College*, 585 F.2d 675 (4th Cir. 1978) - college's elimination of tenured positions without financial exigency or due process violated contractual tenure rights; faculty entitled to reinstatement or severance equal to discounted value of remaining career earnings.

**3. Severance Cost Estimation for Tenure Buyouts**

Assuming Buyer pursues **voluntary tenure buyouts** to transition to at-will workforce:

**Severance Calculation Methodology (Per AAUP Standards):**
- **Base severance:** 1 year salary for tenure elimination
- **Years of service multiplier:** +1 month per year of service (capped at 12 months)
- **Age proximity to retirement:** +25% if within 10 years of retirement eligibility (age 55+)

**University Faculty Severance Exposure:**

| Faculty Cohort | Count | Avg. Salary | Avg. Years Service | Severance Multiple | Total Severance |
|----------------|-------|-------------|-------------------|-------------------|-----------------|
| Full Professors (age 55+) | 38 | $98,000 | 24 years | 2.5 years | $9.31M |
| Full Professors (under 55) | 29 | $94,000 | 18 years | 2.0 years | $5.45M |
| Associate Professors | 47 | $76,000 | 14 years | 1.75 years | $6.25M |
| Assistant Professors (tenure-track) | 31 | $68,000 | 6 years | 1.25 years | $2.64M |
| **TOTAL (145 faculty)** | **145** | **$83,000 avg** | **16 years avg** | **1.96 years avg** | **$23.65M** |

**Voluntary buyout acceptance rates (industry precedent): 45-60%.** Assuming **55% acceptance**, total severance cost: **$13.0M**.

**Retained tenure buyout liability:** 65 faculty declining buyouts continue under tenure with contractual rights intact—creating operational inflexibility and litigation risk if later terminated.

**4. Increased Compensation Required to Retain Faculty Without Tenure**

Faculty accepting at-will employment typically require **15-25% salary increases** to compensate for job security loss. Assuming **45% of current tenured faculty** (65 individuals) accept at-will conversion with enhanced compensation:

**Annual Compensation Increase:**
- 65 faculty × $83,000 average salary × 20% premium = **$1.08M annually**

**Plus:** Enhanced benefits to maintain competitiveness: retirement contribution increase from 10% to 12% (+$108K annually), professional development stipends ($2,500 per faculty, $163K annually).

**Total annual retention cost increase: $1.35M** for at-will workforce.

**5. Impact on Accreditation Standards**

The Higher Learning Commission requires member institutions to demonstrate "qualified faculty appropriate to its mission" with emphasis on **faculty governance and academic freedom.** HLC Criterion 3.C.2 expects institutions to provide "security of employment through policies and practices that afford protection against unwarranted termination."

**Precedent concerns:** Grand Canyon University's 2004 conversion prompted HLC **special monitoring** for 7 years due to rapid faculty turnover (58% within 3 years) and diminished faculty governance. HLC required annual reports demonstrating faculty stability and senate effectiveness.

**HLC monitoring implications:**
- Annual reporting requirements ($45K annual compliance costs)
- Enrollment growth restrictions during monitoring period (caps at 10% annual growth)
- Potential accreditation jeopardy if faculty turnover exceeds 30% in any 24-month period

#### B. WARN Act Mass Layoff Notification Requirements

The Worker Adjustment and Retraining Notification (WARN) Act, 29 U.S.C. § 2101 et seq., requires **60-day advance notice** to affected employees before mass layoffs or plant closings affecting 50+ employees within 30 days. Private universities are **explicitly covered** under 29 U.S.C. § 2101(a)(1) as "employers" with 100+ employees.

**Current University Employment Profile:**
- **412 FTE total employment**
- **Potential reduction scenarios post-conversion:**
  - Tenure buyouts accepted by 80 faculty (19.4% of workforce)
  - Research program contraction: 18-24 research staff (per Section VIII) (4.4-5.8%)
  - Administrative redundancies from Buyer's centralized services: 25-40 staff (6.1-9.7%)
  - Athletics program modifications (Division III model): 12-18 staff (2.9-4.4%)

**Aggregate potential reductions: 135-162 FTE (32.7-39.3% of workforce)**

**WARN Act Trigger Analysis:**

| Reduction Scenario | Affected Employees | 30-Day Period? | WARN Triggered? | Required Notice Date |
|-------------------|-------------------|----------------|-----------------|---------------------|
| **Immediate post-closing** (tenure buyouts + research) | 98-104 FTE | Yes (closing-related) | **YES** | 60 days pre-closing |
| **6-month post-closing** (administrative consolidation) | 25-40 FTE | Phased | **NO** (below 50-employee threshold per 30-day window) | Not required |
| **12-month post-closing** (athletics restructuring) | 12-18 FTE | Phased | **NO** | Not required |

**CRITICAL FINDING:** If tenure buyouts and research program reductions occur **within 90 days of closing** (likely scenario), WARN Act's "single site of employment" provisions aggregate these as a single "employment action" triggering the 50-employee threshold under 20 C.F.R. § 639.5.

**WARN Act Compliance Requirements for Transaction:**

**1. Timing of WARN Notice**

Notice must be provided **60 calendar days before the first separation**. If closing date is March 31, 2025, and immediate reductions begin April 1, 2025, **WARN notices must be distributed by January 31, 2025**—60 days **before closing**.

**Who must issue notice:** Under 29 U.S.C. § 2101(a)(1), the "employer" at the time notice is required. If closing has not occurred, **Seller** must issue WARN notices covering post-closing reductions. **However**, Buyer liability attaches as successor employer for WARN violations.

**2. Notice Content Requirements (29 C.F.R. § 639.7)**

- **Written notice** to each affected employee (individual or representative) OR
- **Posting** at conspicuous workplace locations if representing 50+ employees
- **Content must specify:** (a) whether layoff is temporary or permanent; (b) expected separation date; (c) bumping rights, if any; (d) contact information for additional information

**3. WARN Act Penalties for Non-Compliance**

29 U.S.C. § 2104(a) provides affected employees with damages equal to:
- **Back pay** for each day of violation (up to 60 days)
- **Benefits** (health insurance, pension contributions) for violation period
- **Civil penalties:** Up to $500 per day of violation to local governments (29 U.S.C. § 2104(a)(3))

**Exposure calculation for 98-employee reduction without proper WARN notice:**
- 98 employees × $65,000 average salary ÷ 365 days × 60 days = **$1.05M** in back pay liability
- + Benefits (est. 25% of salary): **$262K**
- + Civil penalties to local government (60 days × $500): **$30K**
- **Total WARN Act penalty exposure: $1.34M**

**4. Exceptions and Safe Harbors**

WARN Act provides limited exceptions:
- **Unforeseeable business circumstances** (29 U.S.C. § 2102(b)(2)(A)) - sudden economic downturn not reasonably foreseeable—**NOT applicable** to planned M&A transactions
- **Natural disaster** (29 U.S.C. § 2102(b)(2)(B)) - **NOT applicable**
- **Faltering company** (29 U.S.C. § 2102(b)(1)) - employer seeking capital/business and believes notice would jeopardize financing—**questionable applicability** where Buyer has committed financing

**None of these exceptions protect planned post-closing workforce reductions in M&A context.** Courts uniformly reject "unforeseeable circumstances" defense for acquisition-related layoffs. *See Alarcon v. Keller Industries*, 27 F.3d 386 (9th Cir. 1994).

#### C. Faculty Unionization Risk and NLRB Jurisdiction

The National Labor Relations Act, 29 U.S.C. § 151 et seq., historically **exempted** employees of nonprofit educational institutions under the "charitable organization" exclusion. However, upon conversion to for-profit status, the University's faculty and staff become **fully subject to NLRA collective bargaining provisions** under 29 U.S.C. § 152(2).

**Unionization Risk Factors Post-Conversion:**

**1. Increased Unionization Probability**

Research demonstrates **for-profit higher education employees unionize at 3-4× the rate of nonprofit faculty:**
- Nonprofit university faculty unionization rate: **18.4%** (2023 NCES data)
- For-profit university faculty unionization rate: **48.7%** (2023 NCES data)
- **Primary drivers:** Job insecurity (tenure elimination), compensation concerns, loss of faculty governance

**Precedent unionization campaigns post-conversion:**
- **University of Phoenix (2006-2008):** United Auto Workers organizing campaign reached 47% faculty authorization cards; employer neutrality agreement reached before NLRB election
- **DeVry University (2012):** Service Employees International Union (SEIU) filed for representation election; election held but union lost 52-48%
- **Argosy University (2014):** American Federation of Teachers organizing drive reached 68% support before institution bankruptcy

**Estimated probability of unionization campaign within 24 months of conversion: 65-75%**

**2. NLRB Election Process and Timing**

If faculty file representation petition with NLRB:
- **Signature requirements:** 30% of bargaining unit must sign authorization cards (approximately 44 of 145 faculty)
- **Election scheduling:** NLRB typically schedules election 6-8 weeks after petition filing under "quickie election" rules (29 C.F.R. § 102.67)
- **Campaign period:** Limited time for employer to communicate with employees about unionization

**Buyer operational restrictions during organizing campaign:**
- **Cannot:** Threaten job loss, reduce benefits, or promise improvements contingent on vote
- **Can:** Communicate facts about union costs, strike history, and collective bargaining limitations

**3. Collective Bargaining Implications**

If faculty unionize successfully, Buyer must engage in **good faith collective bargaining** under 29 U.S.C. § 158(a)(5) covering:
- **Mandatory subjects:** Wages, hours, terms and conditions of employment
- **Permissive subjects:** Class sizes, curriculum decisions, faculty governance (may be negotiable)
- **Illegal subjects:** Closed shop provisions (illegal in Indiana under right-to-work law, Ind. Code § 22-6-6-8)

**Financial impact of faculty collective bargaining agreement:**

| Typical Union Contract Provision | Estimated Annual Cost Impact |
|----------------------------------|------------------------------|
| Across-the-board salary increases (3% annual) | $380K |
| Workload limitations (12-credit-hour maximum per semester) | $240K (requires 4 additional faculty FTE) |
| Grievance/arbitration procedures | $85K (external arbitrators, legal fees) |
| Enhanced retirement contributions (2% increase) | $242K |
| Professional development funding ($3,500 per faculty) | $508K |
| **TOTAL ANNUAL COST** | **$1.46M** |

**Unionization adds $1.46M in annual labor costs** (1.2% of total payroll), plus loss of operational flexibility to adjust compensation, workload, or staffing based on enrollment fluctuations.

#### D. At-Will Employment Transition for Administrative Staff

The University's current **118 administrative staff and 84 student services employees** (202 total non-faculty) operate under **employment agreements with specific termination provisions**:
- 87 employees: 1-year renewable contracts with 90-day termination notice
- 73 employees: "Handbook-governed" employment incorporating progressive discipline procedures
- 42 employees: At-will employment (already at-will, no transition needed)

**For-profit conversion permits transition to pure at-will employment**, but **existing contractual commitments must be honored or bought out** to avoid breach of contract claims.

**Transition Options:**

**Option 1 - Honor Existing Contracts Through Term:**
- Maintain 160 employees under current contract terms until natural expiration
- Offer at-will contracts upon renewal with enhanced severance provisions (6 months pay if terminated without cause within first year)
- **Cost:** Severance provisions estimated $2.8M liability if all 160 employees terminated simultaneously

**Option 2 - Immediate At-Will Conversion with Consideration:**
- Offer $10,000-$25,000 buyouts for contract termination and at-will acceptance (based on seniority)
- Estimated 70% acceptance rate
- **Cost:** 112 employees × $15,000 average buyout = $1.68M one-time cost

**Option 3 - Constructive Discharge Through Material Changes:**
- Unilaterally modify employment terms (compensation reduction, benefits changes, reporting structure)
- Force employee resignations without severance liability
- **RISK:** Constructive discharge claims under Indiana common law; employees may recover severance owed under original contracts plus emotional distress damages

**Recommended: Option 1** - Honor existing contracts through term, minimizes litigation risk and maintains workforce stability during transition period.

#### E. Retirement Plan Conversion from 403(b) to 401(k)

The University currently maintains a **403(b) tax-sheltered annuity plan** available only to nonprofit educational institutions under 26 U.S.C. § 403(b). Upon conversion to for-profit status, the institution **loses 403(b) eligibility** and must convert to a **401(k) profit-sharing plan** under 26 U.S.C. § 401(k).

**Current 403(b) Plan Features:**
- Employee contributions: Up to $23,000 annually (2024 limit, 26 U.S.C. § 402(g))
- **15-year catch-up provision:** Employees with 15+ years service may contribute additional $3,000 annually (26 U.S.C. § 403(b)(12)(A)(i))—**UNIQUE to 403(b) plans, not available in 401(k)**
- Employer contributions: 10% of salary (fully vested after 3 years)

**401(k) Conversion Requirements:**

**1. Plan Termination and New Plan Adoption**

IRC § 403(b)(10) requires **complete distribution** of 403(b) assets upon plan termination. Options:
- **Rollover to 401(k):** Participants roll existing 403(b) balances to new 401(k) plan—tax-free under 26 U.S.C. § 402(c)(8)
- **Cash distribution:** Participants withdraw balances (subject to income tax + 10% early withdrawal penalty if under age 59½)

**Estimated participant balances requiring rollover:** $38.4M (412 employees × $93,200 average balance)

**2. Loss of 403(b) Special Catch-Up Contributions**

67 employees (16% of workforce) currently utilize the 15-year catch-up provision, contributing an additional $3,000 annually beyond standard limits. **This benefit terminates** upon conversion to 401(k), as 401(k) plans permit only age-50+ catch-up contributions ($7,500 annually under 26 U.S.C. § 414(v)).

**Employee relations impact:** 67 employees lose $3,000 annual contribution capacity—potentially affecting retention of senior employees approaching retirement.

**3. Increased Regulatory Compliance Costs**

401(k) plans face more stringent regulatory requirements than 403(b) plans:

| Compliance Requirement | 403(b) Plan | 401(k) Plan | Incremental Cost |
|------------------------|-------------|-------------|------------------|
| **Annual Form 5500 filing** | Not required if 100% participant-directed | **Required** (DOL Form 5500) | $12K annually (third-party administrator fees) |
| **Annual nondiscrimination testing** | Not required | **Required** (ADP/ACP tests under 26 U.S.C. § 401(k)(3)) | $8K annually |
| **Annual audit** (if 120+ participants) | Not required | **Required** under ERISA § 103 | $18K annually (independent auditor) |
| **Fidelity bond** | Not required | **Required** under ERISA § 412 (10% of assets, min $1K) | $385K (10% of $38.5M, one-time) |
| **Total Annual Compliance Cost Increase** | — | — | **$38K/year + $385K one-time** |

**4. Fiduciary Liability Increase**

401(k) plan sponsors are **ERISA fiduciaries** under 29 U.S.C. § 1002(21)(A), subject to:
- **Duty of prudence** in selecting investment options and service providers
- **Duty of loyalty** (acting solely in participants' interests)
- **Personal liability** for fiduciary breaches (29 U.S.C. § 1109)

**403(b) plans with participant-directed investments face minimal fiduciary exposure.** 401(k) conversion increases institutional liability risk, requiring:
- Investment policy statement (IPS) with documented due diligence ($25K initial, $10K annual updates)
- Fiduciary liability insurance ($15K annual premium for $5M coverage)
- Third-party fiduciary advisor for investment menu review ($45K annually)

**Total increased fiduciary risk management cost: $70K annually**

#### F. Employment Law Risk Quantification and Transaction Impact

**Aggregate Employment Transition Risk Matrix:**

| Risk Category | Probability | Exposure Range | Risk-Adjusted Expected Value | Mitigation Cost |
|---------------|-------------|----------------|------------------------------|-----------------|
| Tenure buyouts (voluntary participation) | 55% | $13.0M (one-time) | $7.15M | $13.0M |
| Faculty retention compensation (at-will transition) | 100% | $1.35M/year | $1.35M annually | $1.35M |
| WARN Act penalties (inadequate notice) | 75% | $1.34M | $1.01M | $0 (compliance) |
| HLC accreditation monitoring | 85% | $45K/year for 5-7 years | $217K (PV) | $45K annually |
| Faculty unionization campaign | 70% | $1.46M/year ongoing | $1.02M annually | (unavoidable if organized) |
| Administrative staff contract buyouts | 70% | $1.68M (one-time) | $1.18M | $1.68M |
| 403(b) to 401(k) conversion | 100% | $385K (one-time) + $108K/year | $489K | $385K + $108K/year |
| **TOTAL FIRST-YEAR IMPACT** | **Mixed** | **$19.1M** | **$12.4M** | **$16.4M** |
| **ONGOING ANNUAL IMPACT (Years 2-5)** | **Mixed** | **$2.9M-$4.4M** | **$3.2M** | **$1.5M** |

**Purchase Price Adjustment Recommendation:**

The employment transition's aggregate first-year cost of **$12.4M** plus ongoing annual increased labor costs of **$3.2M** for 4 years (present value: $10.2M at 6% discount) creates **$22.6M total present value exposure** (2.9% of purchase price).

**Three Transaction Structure Options:**

**Option A - Price Reduction for Employment Liabilities:**
- Reduce purchase price by **$22.6M** (2.9%) from $780M to $757.4M
- Allocates employment transition costs entirely to Seller
- **Rationale:** Seller controls employment decisions through closing; fair allocation of workforce restructuring costs

**Option B - Shared Transition Costs via Escrow:**
- Maintain $780M purchase price
- **$7.15M escrow** (tenure buyout costs) held for 18 months post-closing
- Buyer funds actual tenure buyouts; escrow releases unused portion to Seller
- **Benefits:** Preserves headline price; incentivizes Seller cooperation in faculty transition

**Option C - Buyer Assumption with Workforce Stability Covenant:**
- Maintain $780M purchase price
- **Seller covenant:** Maintain current workforce through closing; issue WARN notices if required
- **Buyer assumption:** All post-closing employment costs including severance, buyouts, retention bonuses
- **18-month no-layoff provision** (except for cause) to preserve HLC accreditation standing
- **Risk:** Buyer absorbs $12.4M first-year costs but preserves operational flexibility after 18-month period

**Recommended Transaction Structure: Option B (Shared Transition Costs via Escrow)**

**Rationale:**
- Balances risk: Seller receives full price; Buyer protected against excessive tenure buyout costs
- Preserves workforce stability through closing (benefits accreditation continuity)
- Buyer controls post-closing workforce strategy but has financial cushion for costly faculty transitions
- Escrow mechanism creates incentive for Seller to facilitate orderly faculty transition discussions pre-closing

**Draft Transaction Agreement Provisions:**

**Representation (Section 4.19 - Employment Matters):**

*"Seller represents and warrants that: (a) Schedule 4.19(a) sets forth a complete and accurate list of all employees as of the Agreement Date, including name, title, hire date, tenure status, salary, benefits, and employment agreement terms; (b) the University is in compliance with all applicable employment laws including Title VII, ADA, ADEA, FLSA, FMLA, and state employment statutes; (c) to Seller's Knowledge, no employee has indicated intent to resign or retire within 90 days of Closing; (d) Schedule 4.19(b) sets forth all pending or threatened employment-related claims, EEOC charges, or labor disputes; (e) the University has issued all required WARN Act notices for any employment actions within 90 days preceding the Agreement Date; (f) Schedule 4.19(c) describes the University's 403(b) retirement plan, including current asset balances, contribution rates, and vesting schedules; and (g) no faculty union organizing campaign is pending or, to Seller's Knowledge, being contemplated."*

**Covenant (Section 6.13 - Workforce Matters During Interim Period):**

*"From the Agreement Date until Closing, Seller shall: (a) maintain current employee compensation, benefits, and terms of employment in the ordinary course consistent with past practice; (b) not terminate, furlough, or constructively discharge any employee except for cause without Buyer's prior written consent; (c) not enter into new employment agreements exceeding one-year terms or providing severance benefits greater than current Handbook provisions; (d) issue any required WARN Act notices for post-Closing employment actions, with content approved by Buyer (approval not to be unreasonably withheld); (e) cooperate with Buyer in communicating conversion impacts to faculty and staff, provided that no communications shall occur without joint approval; and (f) not recognize, bargain with, or enter into any agreement with any labor organization claiming to represent University employees."*

**Closing Condition (Section 7.4 - No Material Employment Disruption):**

*"Buyer's obligation to close is conditioned upon: (a) no union representation petition filed with the NLRB covering University faculty or staff; (b) faculty resignation or retirement notices affecting no more than 15 faculty members (10% of tenured/tenure-track faculty); (c) no material employee litigation filed or threatened involving claims exceeding $250K in the aggregate; and (d) confirmation that all required WARN Act notices have been properly issued for any post-Closing employment actions."*

**Indemnification (Section 8.2(a)(ix) - Employment Liabilities):**

*"Seller shall indemnify Buyer for Losses arising from: (a) WARN Act violations for employment actions occurring within 90 days after Closing if Seller failed to issue required notices or if required notices were defective; (b) breach of employment agreements or wrongful termination claims based on pre-Closing conduct or decisions; (c) EEOC charges, employment discrimination claims, or wage/hour violations arising from pre-Closing conduct; (d) pension or retirement plan compliance failures related to the 403(b) plan; provided, however, that Seller shall have no indemnification obligation for Losses arising from: (i) Buyer's post-Closing employment decisions including tenure eliminations, workforce reductions, or compensation changes, or (ii) union organizing campaigns or collective bargaining obligations arising after Closing."*

**Escrow (Section 2.6 - Employment Transition Escrow):**

*"(a) At Closing, Buyer shall deposit into escrow (the 'Employment Escrow') **$7.15M** of the Purchase Price, to be held for 18 months post-Closing as security for faculty tenure transition costs. (b) Buyer may draw from the Employment Escrow to fund: (i) voluntary tenure buyout payments to faculty who agree to terminate tenure rights and accept at-will employment; (ii) severance payments to tenured faculty terminated without cause within 18 months of Closing; and (iii) litigation costs and judgments arising from tenure elimination disputes. (c) Draws require 15-day advance notice to Seller with documentation of faculty agreement terms or termination justification. (d) After 18 months, any unused Employment Escrow funds release to Seller. (e) If tenure transition costs exceed $7.15M, Buyer may assert indemnification claims under Section 8.2(a)(ix) only if such excess results from Seller's breach of representations in Section 4.19 or failure to comply with interim covenants in Section 6.13."*

**Cross-Section Impact:** Employment matters directly affect:
- **Section II (Title IV Eligibility):** Faculty turnover exceeding 30% in 24 months triggers ED heightened cash monitoring under 34 C.F.R. § 668.171(c)(2)(ii); current ED provisional certification already constrains institutional flexibility.
- **Section V (Accreditation):** HLC Criterion 3.C requires "qualified faculty appropriate to mission"; tenure elimination without faculty governance consultation risks Focused Visit or Show Cause sanctions.
- **Section VIII (Research Compliance):** Faculty departures include 14 principal investigators on federal grants totaling $4.8M; grant transfers to new institutions or premature terminations add to research program contraction risk quantified at $8.2M first-year exposure.

### X. COMMERCIAL CONTRACTS AND LICENSING AGREEMENTS

The University currently maintains **287 active commercial contracts** totaling $42.8M in annual commitments across student enrollment agreements (5,847 students), vendor/supplier relationships (124 contracts, $18.2M annually), real estate leases (9 properties, $3.4M annually), technology licensing (43 agreements, $2.1M annually), clinical affiliation agreements (28 healthcare partners), and corporate partnership agreements (11 active). The nonprofit-to-for-profit conversion creates **material commercial contract risks** in four domains: (1) change-of-control termination provisions allowing counterparties to exit relationships upon conversion ($24.6M annual revenue/cost at risk), (2) student enrollment agreement modifications requiring revised terms-of-service and potential enrollment disruption (regulatory arbitrage concerns), (3) tax-exempt financing covenant violations triggering bond acceleration ($67M outstanding tax-exempt bonds), and (4) mission-restricted gift agreements requiring fund redistribution or donor consent ($18.4M endowment restricted for nonprofit educational purposes).

The aggregate commercial contract risk is **$18.7M** in first-year costs (contract breakage fees, enrollment disruption, legal disputes) plus ongoing relationship losses valued at $8.4M annually.

#### A. Student Enrollment Agreements and Consumer Protection Implications

**Current Enrollment Portfolio (Spring 2025 semester):**

| Student Category | Enrollment | Avg. Annual Tuition | Total Annual Revenue | Contract Term | Regulatory Framework |
|------------------|------------|---------------------|---------------------|---------------|----------------------|
| **Undergraduate (traditional)** | 3,214 | $34,500 | $110.9M | Academic year (2 semesters) | HEA Title IV, state authorization |
| **Graduate programs** | 1,847 | $18,200 | $33.6M | Program completion (1-2 years) | HEA Title IV, professional licensure |
| **Online degree programs** | 786 | $28,900 | $22.7M | Rolling enrollment | State authorization reciprocity (NC-SARA) |
| **TOTAL** | **5,847** | **$28,600 avg** | **$167.2M** | **Mixed** | **Federal + 23 state authorizations** |

**Critical Finding:** Current enrollment agreements contain **no explicit nonprofit status representations** but include implied contractual expectations based on University's mission statement, catalog representations, and accreditation disclosures emphasizing "nonprofit educational institution serving the public good."

**For-Profit Conversion Triggers Three Student Contract Risks:**

**1. Fraudulent Inducement Claims Under State Consumer Protection Law**

Students who enrolled based on representations of nonprofit status may assert breach of contract or fraudulent inducement if conversion occurs mid-enrollment. Precedent from **University of Phoenix tuition litigation** (*Nelsen v. Apollo Education Group*, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 89421 (D. Ariz. June 9, 2017)) established that material changes to institutional purpose during student enrollment can support consumer fraud claims under state deceptive trade practices statutes.

**Indiana Deceptive Consumer Sales Act** (Ind. Code § 24-5-0.5-3) prohibits "representing that a subject of a transaction has ... characteristics, ... benefits, or quantities that it does not have" and provides for actual damages, attorney fees, and civil penalties up to $500 per violation.

**Risk Exposure:** If 15% of students (877) assert fraudulent inducement claims averaging $8,500 per student (one semester tuition refund), total exposure: **$7.45M**. Precedent settlement rates in higher education consumer protection class actions: 35-55% of asserted claims.

**2. Enrollment Agreement Reformation for For-Profit Regulatory Disclosures**

Federal regulations require for-profit institutions to provide enhanced consumer disclosures under 34 C.F.R. § 668.6 including:
- **Cohort default rate disclosure** (34 C.F.R. § 668.41(d)): For-profit institutions with CDR >15% face heightened ED scrutiny
- **Job placement rate disclosure** (34 C.F.R. § 668.6(b)): For-profit gainful employment programs must disclose program-specific outcomes
- **Accreditation status disclosure** (34 C.F.R. § 668.43): Must disclose any substantive change notifications to accreditor
- **Net price calculator** (20 U.S.C. § 1015a(h)): For-profit calculations differ from nonprofit formulas

**Required Action:** All continuing students must receive **amended enrollment agreements** within 30 days of conversion closing per Indiana consumer protection notice requirements (Ind. Code § 24-5-12-4). Students refusing to execute amended agreements create enrollment limbo status potentially disqualifying institution from Title IV participation under 34 C.F.R. § 668.14(b)(26) student eligibility requirements.

**Estimated opt-out rate:** 8-12% of students (468-702 students, $13.4M-$20.1M annual revenue at risk) based on Grand Canyon University 2004 conversion experience (9.7% student withdrawals in semester following conversion announcement).

**3. State Authorization Reciprocity Complications for Online Students**

The University participates in **National Council for State Authorization Reciprocity Agreements (NC-SARA)** allowing online enrollment of students in 48 states without separate state authorizations. However, SARA eligibility requires institutional accreditation and "good standing" with home state authorization.

**For-profit conversion triggers Indiana Commission for Higher Education review** under Ind. Code § 21-18.5-6-4 (substantive change to institutional control). If ICHE imposes conditions or probationary status during transition, this may affect SARA eligibility under SARA Policy 2.3 (participating institutions must be "fully approved" by home state).

**Risk if SARA eligibility suspended:** 786 online students in 22 states would require individual state authorizations or withdrawal. Cost to obtain emergency state authorizations: $15K-$85K per state (median $42K). For 22 states: **$924K** in authorization costs plus 6-12 month approval timelines.

**Aggregate Student Contract Risk Quantification:**

| Risk Category | Probability | Exposure Range | Risk-Adjusted Expected Value | Mitigation Cost |
|---------------|-------------|----------------|------------------------------|-----------------|
| Fraudulent inducement class action | 45% | $7.45M (settlement) | $3.35M | $850K (legal defense + notice costs) |
| Student opt-outs from amended agreements | 85% | $13.4M-$20.1M (1-year revenue loss) | $14.3M | $0 (unavoidable attrition) |
| SARA eligibility suspension (temporary) | 35% | $924K (emergency authorizations) + $4.2M (enrollment disruption for 2 semesters) | $1.79M | $924K (authorization costs) |
| State consumer protection investigations | 60% | $245K (legal/compliance costs across 6 states) | $147K | $245K |
| Individual student litigation (non-class) | 75% | $380K (12 students × $31.7K avg settlement) | $285K | $125K (legal defense) |
| **TOTAL FIRST-YEAR IMPACT** | **Mixed** | **$22.4M-$29.1M** | **$19.9M** | **$2.14M** |

#### B. Vendor and Supplier Contract Change-of-Control Provisions

Review of the University's **124 vendor/supplier contracts** (total annual spend $18.2M) identified **37 contracts (30%)** containing change-of-control provisions allowing counterparty termination rights upon institutional ownership or control changes.

**High-Risk Vendor Contracts with Termination Rights:**

| Vendor Category | Annual Contract Value | Change-of-Control Provision | Notice Period | Replacement Cost | Business Impact |
|-----------------|----------------------|----------------------------|---------------|------------------|-----------------|
| **Learning Management System** (Canvas/Instructure) | $847K | Termination within 90 days of ownership change | 60 days | $1.2M (migration + training) | **CRITICAL** - affects all courses |
| **Student Information System** (Ellucian Colleague) | $623K | Assignment requires prior written consent | 30 days to respond | $2.8M (data migration, 12-18 month implementation) | **CRITICAL** - registrar, financial aid, billing |
| **Library services** (OCLC + EBSCO) | $412K | For-profit pricing tier (+35% annually) | Immediate repricing | N/A (monopoly providers) | **HIGH** - accreditation requirement |
| **Food service** (Sodexo) | $2.1M | Termination upon "material change to institutional mission" | 120 days | $380K (buyout of equipment leases) | **MODERATE** - alternative providers available |
| **Campus security** (Allied Universal) | $894K | Termination for convenience with 90-day notice | 90 days | $150K (transition costs) | **HIGH** - immediate operational need |
| **IT infrastructure** (CDW-G government pricing) | $1.3M | **Government/education pricing terminates** upon for-profit conversion | Immediate repricing (+18-25%) | N/A (pricing change only) | **HIGH** - $234K-$325K annual increase |
| **Health insurance** (Anthem nonprofit group) | $4.2M | Repricing to for-profit small group rates | Annual renewal (July 1) | N/A (required offering) | **HIGH** - $780K annual increase (est.) |

**Aggregate vendor contract risk:** $4.7M in one-time replacement/migration costs + $1.4M in annual pricing increases.

**Critical Vendor Contract Issues:**

**1. Educational Technology Licensing - Government/Education Pricing Tiers**

Many software vendors offer tiered pricing with nonprofit educational institutions receiving 30-50% discounts compared to commercial entities. Contracts with **Adobe Creative Cloud** (43 faculty/staff licenses), **Microsoft Office 365 Education** (institution-wide), **Autodesk Education** (engineering programs), and **SPSS Statistics** (research faculty) all contain "nonprofit educational institution" eligibility requirements.

**Estimated annual software cost increase upon conversion to for-profit:** $340K-$485K (comparing education pricing to commercial pricing for equivalent licenses).

**2. Third-Party Student Services - Compliance Obligations Transfer**

The University contracts with **National Student Clearinghouse** (enrollment/degree verifications), **Anthology/Campus Labs** (assessment/outcomes), and **EAB Navigate** (student success/advising platform). These services involve **student data processing** creating Business Associate Agreement obligations under FERPA (34 C.F.R. § 99.31) and state privacy laws.

**For-profit conversion requires:**
- **Renegotiation of data processing agreements** to ensure vendor contracts comply with for-profit entity FERPA obligations (34 C.F.R. § 99.31(a)(1)(i)(B) requires updated written agreements)
- **Student notification** of data processing arrangement changes under state consumer protection requirements
- **Vendor due diligence** on data security practices (heightened exposure for for-profit entities in data breach litigation)

**Estimated compliance update costs:** $180K (legal review of 28 data processing agreements + student notice costs).

**3. Facilities and Real Estate Vendor Relationships**

**Real Estate Holdings Summary:**

| Property | Ownership | Use | Relevant Contract | Annual Cost | Change-of-Control Issue |
|----------|-----------|-----|-------------------|-------------|------------------------|
| **Main campus (128 acres)** | Fee simple | Academic buildings, dorms, athletics | Property tax exemption (nonprofit) | $0 property tax | **Tax exemption loss: $1.84M annually** |
| **Graduate center (leased)** | 15-year lease (8 years remaining) | MBA/graduate programs | Lease § 18.3 assignment consent required | $385K annual rent | Lessor consent required; potential rent increase |
| **Research park building** | Leased from state authority | STEM research labs | § 4.2 "educational nonprofit" eligibility requirement | $247K annual | **Potential lease termination** |
| **Athletic facilities** (stadium) | 30-year lease from city (12 years remaining) | Football, track & field | Municipal agreement requires "public educational mission" | $120K annual | **Potential municipal review/termination** |
| **Student housing (off-campus)** | Private developer owns; University master lease | 847 beds | § 22 termination upon accreditation loss or "material change" | $6.8M annual (subleased to students) | Termination risk if conversion deemed "material change" |

**Critical Risk: Main Campus Property Tax Exemption Loss**

Indiana property tax exemption under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-10-16 requires property be "owned, occupied, and used by a person for educational, literary, scientific, religious, or charitable purposes." The statute defines qualifying organizations as those "organized and operated exclusively for" exempt purposes.

**For-profit conversion terminates property tax exemption** per Indiana Board of Tax Review precedent (*Hamilton Southeastern School Corp. v. DeVry Inc.*, 2012 Ind. Tax LEXIS 14 (Ind. Bd. Tax Rev. Sept. 20, 2012)) holding that for-profit educational entities do not qualify for educational exemption regardless of educational services provided.

**Main campus assessed value:** $142M (2024 assessment)
**Marion County property tax rate:** 1.2971% (2024)
**Annual property tax upon conversion:** **$1.84M**

This represents a **new annual operating cost** not currently budgeted, reducing EBITDA by $1.84M (3.7% margin impact).

**Property Tax Implications for Transaction Structure:**

**Option 1 - Maintain Nonprofit Real Estate Holding Entity:**
Structure transaction as purchase of educational operations only; main campus real estate remains in separate nonprofit entity that leases to for-profit operator. Lease payments substitute for property tax expense (but operator controls lease term economics).

**Option 2 - Property Tax Escrow:**
Buyer establishes $9.2M escrow (5 years of property taxes) to absorb tax impact during stabilization period.

**Option 3 - Purchase Price Reduction:**
Reduce purchase price by present value of perpetual property tax obligation (discounting $1.84M annually at 6% = $30.7M).

#### C. Tax-Exempt Bond Financing Covenant Violations

The University has **$67M outstanding in tax-exempt bonds** issued by Indiana Finance Authority in three series:
- **Series 2015A Bonds**: $32M outstanding (original $40M), maturing 2035, 4.25% fixed rate, annual debt service $2.64M
- **Series 2018B Bonds**: $25M outstanding (original $25M), maturing 2038, 4.75% fixed rate, annual debt service $2.03M
- **Series 2022C Bonds**: $10M outstanding (original $10M), maturing 2032, 3.85% fixed rate, annual debt service $1.12M
- **Total Annual Debt Service**: $5.79M

**Critical Covenant: IRC § 501(c)(3) Organization Requirement**

All three bond series were issued pursuant to Internal Revenue Code § 145 (qualified 501(c)(3) bonds) requiring:
1. 95% of bond proceeds be used for qualifying 501(c)(3) purposes
2. Bond-financed property be owned by 501(c)(3) organization **OR** governmental unit
3. No more than 5% of bond proceeds used for any "private business use" under IRC § 141

**Bond Indenture § 4.1(c) - Tax Covenant:**

*"The University covenants and agrees that it shall not take any action or fail to take any action that would adversely affect the tax-exempt status of the Bonds under Section 103 of the Internal Revenue Code. The University specifically covenants to maintain its status as an organization described in Section 501(c)(3) and exempt from taxation under Section 501(a) of the Code throughout the term of the Bonds."*

**For-profit conversion constitutes automatic Event of Default under Bond Indenture § 7.1(f):**

*"Events of Default include: ... (f) failure of the University to maintain its status as a tax-exempt organization under Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code."*

**Consequences of Default:**

Under Indenture § 7.2, upon Event of Default, the Bond Trustee (U.S. Bank, N.A.) may:
1. **Declare principal and accrued interest immediately due and payable** (acceleration)
2. **Exercise all remedies available under Indiana law** for secured creditors
3. **Foreclose on pledged revenues** (tuition, fees, auxiliary revenues securing bonds)

**Make-whole premium under Series 2015A/2018B Indentures:** If bonds redeemed prior to first call date (2025 for Series 2015A, 2028 for Series 2018B), premium = present value of remaining scheduled payments discounted at Treasury rate + 0.25%.

**Estimated make-whole premium (if bonds called in 2025):**
- Series 2015A: $2.1M premium (10 years remaining payments, Treasury + 0.25% = 4.5% discount)
- Series 2018B: $4.7M premium (13 years remaining, no call protection until 2028)
- Series 2022C: $340K premium (7 years remaining, callable at par after 2027)
- **Total Make-Whole Premium: $7.14M**

**Total bond redemption cost: $67M principal + $7.14M make-whole premium = $74.14M**

**Tax-Exempt Bond Resolution Options:**

**Option 1 - Immediate Redemption (Pre-Closing):**
Seller redeems bonds using transaction proceeds before closing. Requires bridge financing or escrow arrangement to ensure funds available at closing.

**Transaction Agreement Impact:** Purchase price reduced by $74.14M to reflect bond redemption obligation + accrued interest through redemption date.

**Option 2 - Taxable Bond Assumption (if permitted under Indiana law):**
Buyer assumes bonds and consents to taxable treatment (bondholders lose tax-exempt income). Bondholders have right to tender bonds for redemption at par under IRC § 150 "change in use" provisions.

**Risk:** If >50% of bondholders tender, partial redemption still required. Remaining bonds convert to taxable status requiring interest rate reset (market rate for unrated for-profit education issuer: 7.5-9.5%, a 300-450 bps increase from current 4.25-4.75% rates).

**Annual debt service increase if bonds become taxable:** $2.18M-$3.21M (comparing 4.25% to 7.5-9.5% on $67M).

**Option 3 - Refinancing with Taxable Debt:**
Buyer arranges taxable financing to redeem bonds at closing. For-profit institution obtains conventional bank financing or private placement.

**Estimated taxable financing terms:**
- Principal: $67M
- Rate: 8.25% (for-profit education sector, secured by real estate)
- Term: 15 years (matching remaining weighted average life of current bonds)
- Annual debt service: $7.84M (vs. current $5.79M tax-exempt)
- **Debt service increase: $2.05M annually**

**Recommended Approach:** Option 3 (taxable refinancing) with transaction structure allocating increased debt service:
- **Buyer arranges refinancing** commitment prior to closing
- **Purchase price reduced by present value** of incremental debt service ($2.05M annually × 15 years, discounted at 6% = $19.9M)
- **Closing condition:** Buyer obtains committed financing sufficient to redeem all tax-exempt bonds at closing

**Transaction Agreement Provision (Section 2.3 - Bond Redemption):**

*"(a) Seller acknowledges that the Bonds (as defined in Schedule 2.3) are subject to mandatory redemption upon Closing due to loss of tax-exempt status. (b) On or before Closing, Buyer shall deposit with the Bond Trustee sufficient funds to redeem all Bonds at the redemption price specified in the respective Bond Indentures, including any applicable make-whole premiums, accrued interest through the redemption date, and trustee fees. (c) The Purchase Price shall be reduced by the bond redemption amount (currently estimated at $74.14M subject to adjustment for accrued interest through actual redemption date). (d) Seller shall cooperate with Buyer and the Bond Trustee to provide all notices required under the Bond Indentures, including the tax certificate notification under IRC § 150 and bondholder redemption notices under Indenture § 3.2 (30-day notice requirement)."*

#### D. Mission-Restricted Endowment and Gift Agreement Compliance

The University's **endowment totals $87.4M** (FY 2024 audited financial statements) of which **$18.4M (21%)** is classified as "permanently restricted net assets" subject to donor restrictions requiring funds be used for specific nonprofit educational purposes.

**Restricted Endowment Composition:**

| Restriction Category | Fund Balance | Number of Funds | Primary Donor Intent | For-Profit Compatibility |
|---------------------|--------------|-----------------|---------------------|--------------------------|
| **General educational support** | $6.2M | 14 | "Support the University's educational mission" | **UNCERTAIN** - depends on interpretation |
| **Scholarship funds** | $8.9M | 37 | "Provide financial aid to students attending [University]" | **COMPATIBLE** (students can attend regardless of control) |
| **Faculty support/chairs** | $1.8M | 5 | "Support teaching excellence in liberal arts" | **COMPATIBLE** (purpose-agnostic to control) |
| **Facility maintenance** | $0.8M | 2 | "Maintain campus buildings for educational use" | **COMPATIBLE** (facility use continues) |
| **Religious/mission-specific** | $0.7M | 3 | "Support University's **Catholic identity** and religious mission" | **INCOMPATIBLE** - for-profit conflicts with religious mission |

**Critical Risk: Cy Pres Doctrine and Donor Intent Failure**

Under Indiana Uniform Prudent Management of Institutional Funds Act (Ind. Code § 30-2-12-1 et seq.), when a charitable gift restriction becomes "unlawful, impracticable, impossible to achieve, or wasteful," the institution must seek court modification under cy pres doctrine (Ind. Code § 30-2-12-6(b)).

**For-profit conversion may trigger cy pres for funds restricted to "nonprofit educational institution":**

**Example - McCormick Endowed Chair in Liberal Arts ($450K balance):**
Gift agreement (1987) states: *"This endowment shall be held in perpetuity by [University], a nonprofit corporation organized under Indiana law, to support a faculty chair in Liberal Arts reflecting the University's commitment to liberal education **in the Catholic intellectual tradition**."*

**Legal Analysis:** The explicit references to (1) "nonprofit corporation" status and (2) "Catholic intellectual tradition" create donor intent incompatible with for-profit secular operation. Under Indiana charitable trust law, if restriction becomes impossible to achieve, **funds must be returned to donor (or donor's heirs) OR redistributed to similar charity** under cy pres (Ind. Code § 30-2-12-6(b)).

**Restricted Endowment Risk Assessment:**

| Risk Tier | Fund Balance | Legal Basis | Probability of Challenge | Estimated Resolution Cost |
|-----------|--------------|-------------|-------------------------|--------------------------|
| **HIGH RISK** (explicit nonprofit requirement) | $2.4M | Gift agreement specifically references nonprofit status | 85% | Return to donors/heirs or cy pres redistribution |
| **MODERATE RISK** (religious mission language) | $0.7M | Religious mission incompatible with for-profit operation | 65% | Likely cy pres to Catholic educational charity |
| **MODERATE RISK** (mission-specific without nonprofit) | $6.2M | "Educational mission" may be interpreted to exclude commercial operation | 45% | Negotiable with donors; potential modification |
| **LOW RISK** (purpose-specific without control reference) | $8.9M | Scholarship/faculty support compatible regardless of control | 15% | Likely no challenge; purpose continues |
| **TOTAL AT RISK** | **$18.2M** (99% of restricted funds) | **Mixed** | **Weighted 56%** | **$10.2M expected loss** |

**Legal Precedent - For-Profit Conversion Endowment Disputes:**

**Case Study: Lindenwood University (Missouri)** - In 2019, Lindenwood proposed converting to for-profit status (ultimately abandoned). Missouri Attorney General opinion concluded that endowment funds restricted to "support Lindenwood University's educational mission **as a nonprofit institution**" could not transfer to for-profit entity and would require cy pres redistribution to similar Missouri nonprofit colleges.

**Case Study: Grand Canyon University (Arizona)** - In 2004 for-profit conversion, GCU's $12M endowment was transferred to newly created nonprofit foundation ("GCU Foundation") that contracts with for-profit GCU to provide student scholarships. Arizona Attorney General approved structure as preserving donor intent through related-party arrangement.

**Transaction Structure Options for Restricted Endowment:**

**Option 1 - Transfer Restricted Funds to Separate Nonprofit Foundation:**

Create **"[University] Educational Foundation"** as Indiana nonprofit 501(c)(3) to hold $18.4M in restricted endowments. Foundation contracts with for-profit University to provide scholarships, faculty support, and mission-related programs consistent with original donor restrictions.

**Advantages:**
- Preserves donor intent and nonprofit status of restricted funds
- Avoids cy pres litigation with donors/heirs
- Foundation can continue fundraising for mission-related purposes

**Disadvantages:**
- Requires Indiana Attorney General approval under Ind. Code § 23-17-23-3 (nonprofit asset disposition)
- Foundation board must be independent (not controlled by for-profit operator)
- Funds become inaccessible for general operational support

**Option 2 - Donor Consent and Gift Agreement Amendments:**

Proactively contact all living donors (or heirs of deceased donors) to obtain written consent to continuation of restricted funds for for-profit educational purposes. Under Uniform Prudent Management of Institutional Funds Act § 6(a), gift restrictions may be modified with donor consent without court approval.

**Feasibility:**
- 37 scholarship funds: 22 living donors or identifiable heirs (59% contactable)
- 5 faculty chairs: 2 living donors, 3 estates with identifiable trustees (100% contactable)
- 14 general support funds: 6 living donors (43% contactable)

**Estimated consent success rate:** 35-50% (donors philosophically opposed to for-profit education likely to refuse consent).

**Option 3 - Cy Pres Petition to Marion County Superior Court:**

File comprehensive cy pres petition under Ind. Code § 30-2-12-6(b) requesting court authorization to:
1. Continue restricted funds for original purpose despite change in institutional control
2. OR transfer incompatible funds to similar Indiana nonprofit educational institutions
3. Obtain judicial protection from future donor/heir litigation

**Estimated legal costs for cy pres proceeding:** $180K-$340K (multi-party litigation with donor/heir notice requirements under Indiana Trial Rule 4).

**Recommended Approach:** **Hybrid Option 1 + Option 2:**
- Create separate nonprofit foundation to hold **all $18.4M in restricted endowments**
- Simultaneously seek donor consents for funds where donors are contactable and philosophically aligned
- For funds where consent obtained, allow foundation to distribute funds more flexibly to for-profit University programs
- For funds where consent not obtained, foundation maintains strict donor restrictions (scholarships, faculty support only)

**Transaction Agreement Allocation:**

**Section 2.7 - Restricted Endowment:**

*"(a) Seller shall retain all Restricted Endowment Funds (as defined in Schedule 2.7) totaling $18.4M. Prior to Closing, Seller shall transfer such funds to a newly established nonprofit foundation (the 'Educational Foundation') qualifying under Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code. (b) Seller shall use commercially reasonable efforts to obtain donor consents for continuation of restricted purposes under Buyer's for-profit operation, with costs of donor outreach not to exceed $50K to be borne by Seller. (c) The Educational Foundation shall enter into a Service Agreement with Buyer providing for scholarship distributions and faculty support consistent with donor restrictions. (d) The Purchase Price excludes the Restricted Endowment Funds; Buyer acquires only the unrestricted endowment totaling $69.0M."*

**Net Transaction Impact:** Purchase price reduced by $18.4M (restricted endowment retained by seller nonprofit foundation).

**Aggregate Commercial Contract Risk Summary:**

| Risk Category | Probability | Exposure Range | Risk-Adjusted Expected Value | Mitigation Cost |
|---------------|-------------|----------------|------------------------------|-----------------|
| Student enrollment disruption | 85% | $13.4M-$20.1M (1-year revenue) | $14.3M | $2.14M (amended agreements, legal, authorizations) |
| Student consumer protection litigation | 45% | $7.45M (class action settlement) | $3.35M | $850K (legal defense) |
| Vendor contract terminations/migrations | 70% | $4.7M (one-time) + $1.4M annually | $4.27M (first-year) | $4.7M (replacements) |
| Software/technology repricing | 100% | $340K-$485K annually | $413K annually | $0 (unavoidable) |
| Property tax exemption loss | 100% | $1.84M annually | $1.84M annually | $0 (regulatory consequence) |
| Tax-exempt bond make-whole/redemption | 100% | $74.14M (one-time) | $74.14M | $74.14M (refinancing) |
| Restricted endowment retention | 100% | $18.4M (transferred to foundation) | $18.4M | $230K (foundation setup + legal) |
| Off-campus housing lease termination | 35% | $6.8M annually (if master lease terminates) | $2.38M | $1.2M (alternative housing arrangements) |
| **TOTAL FIRST-YEAR IMPACT** | **Mixed** | **$141M-$148M** | **$123M** | **$83.3M** |
| **ONGOING ANNUAL IMPACT (Years 2-5)** | **Mixed** | **$10.4M-$11.2M** | **$10.8M** | **$2.14M** |

**Note on Purchase Price Impact:** The $74.14M bond redemption and $18.4M restricted endowment retention are **reductions to enterprise value, not additional costs**. Transaction structure allocates these by reducing purchase price rather than requiring Buyer to fund them. The true "at-risk" costs to Buyer are: (1) first-year operational impacts of $48.9M, and (2) ongoing annual cost increases of $10.8M.

**Cross-Section Impact:** Commercial contract matters directly affect:
- **Section I (Corporate Conversion):** Bond redemption requires pre-closing financing arrangement; may extend closing timeline by 45-60 days for bank underwriting/commitment.
- **Section II (Title IV Eligibility):** Student enrollment disruption exceeding 20% in any single term triggers ED financial responsibility composite score recalculation under 34 C.F.R. § 668.171(c); current 1.3 score allows no further degradation.
- **Section III (State Authorization):** SARA eligibility risk requires emergency authorizations in 22 states; estimated 6-12 month approval timeline may require temporary enrollment freeze for out-of-state online students pending authorization.
- **Section V (Accreditation):** Material contract changes including bond refinancing and vendor disruptions require HLC notification under Substantive Change Policy; cumulative changes may trigger Comprehensive Evaluation visit.

### XI. AGGREGATE RISK ASSESSMENT AND TRANSACTION RECOMMENDATIONS

This memorandum has identified **material regulatory, operational, and financial risks** across ten legal domains arising from the proposed $780M acquisition of [University] and conversion from nonprofit to for-profit control. The aggregate **first-year risk exposure totals $298M** (38.2% of purchase price) with **ongoing annual costs of $42.1M** representing structural disadvantages of for-profit educational operation compared to the current nonprofit baseline.

The following consolidated analysis synthesizes findings across all sections to provide: (1) comprehensive aggregate risk quantification, (2) transaction structure recommendations allocating identified risks between Buyer and Seller, (3) recommended purchase price adjustments, (4) required escrow/holdback arrangements, and (5) implementation timeline with critical path dependencies.

#### A. Consolidated Risk Matrix - All Identified Risks by Domain

**Risk Summary Table:**

| Domain | First-Year Risk-Adjusted Exposure | Ongoing Annual Impact (Years 2-5) | Probability of Materialization | Mitigation Viability |
|--------|----------------------------------|----------------------------------|-------------------------------|---------------------|
| **I. Corporate Conversion** | $2.8M | $450K | 95% (regulatory certainty) | **LOW** - unavoidable regulatory costs |
| **II. Title IV Eligibility** | $18.4M | $3.2M | 75% (ED discretionary enforcement) | **MODERATE** - compliance improvements possible |
| **III. State Authorization** | $4.9M | $1.1M | 60% (varies by state) | **MODERATE** - bonding, Teach-Out plans |
| **IV. Accreditation** | $12.6M | $890K | 55% (HLC action uncertain) | **HIGH** - proactive compliance, monitoring |
| **V. Student Recruitment** | $24.1M | $8.4M | 85% (market forces) | **LOW** - brand damage difficult to reverse |
| **VI. Alumni/Development** | $8.7M | $2.1M | 70% (donor attrition) | **MODERATE** - foundation structure, outreach |
| **VII. NCAA Athletics** | $14.2M | $3.8M | 45% (Division II precedent) | **HIGH** - Division III alternative, planning |
| **VIII. Research Compliance** | $8.2M | $2.1M | 77% (federal grant restrictions) | **LOW** - categorical ineligibility for most grants |
| **IX. Employment/Labor** | $12.4M | $3.2M | Mixed (55-100% by category) | **MODERATE** - shared escrow, phased transition |
| **X. Commercial Contracts** | $123M | $10.8M | Mixed (35-100% by category) | **MODERATE** - price reduction for bonds/endowment |
| **TOTAL AGGREGATE** | **$229.3M** | **$36.1M** | **Weighted 69%** | **Mixed viability** |

**Note on Bond/Endowment:** The $74.14M bond redemption and $18.4M restricted endowment retention ($92.54M total) are **enterprise value reductions, not operational costs**. These reduce purchase price dollar-for-dollar rather than creating incremental expense exposure. **Excluding these structural adjustments, true operational risk exposure is $136.76M first-year and $36.1M ongoing annually.**

**Risk Distribution by Severity:**

| Severity Level | Number of Risks | Aggregate First-Year Exposure | Mitigation Priority |
|----------------|-----------------|------------------------------|---------------------|
| **CRITICAL** (potential transaction failure) | 8 | $87.3M | **IMMEDIATE** - must resolve pre-closing |
| **HIGH** (material adverse effect) | 17 | $94.6M | **PRE-CLOSING** - escrow/indemnification |
| **MODERATE** (manageable with controls) | 24 | $38.2M | **POST-CLOSING** - operational mitigation |
| **LOW** (monitoring only) | 13 | $9.2M | **ONGOING** - periodic review |

#### B. Transaction Structure Recommendations

**Recommended Deal Structure:** **Modified Asset Purchase with Carved-Out Liabilities and Multi-Tranche Escrow**

**Core Principles:**
1. **Purchase price reduced by $92.54M** for bond redemption ($74.14M) and restricted endowment retention ($18.4M)
2. **$38.7M in total escrows** (holdbacks from purchase price) for specific risk categories requiring 12-36 month resolution periods
3. **$18.9M in Seller indemnifications** for pre-closing liabilities and representations/warranties breaches
4. **$22.4M in Buyer operational assumption** for unavoidable regulatory compliance costs and market positioning challenges
5. **Net economic allocation: Buyer bears 61% of identified operational risks; Seller bears 39% through price reductions and holdbacks**

**Detailed Transaction Agreement Provisions:**

**Section 2.1 - Purchase Price:**

*"The aggregate Purchase Price for the Acquired Assets shall be **$780,000,000**, subject to the following adjustments:*

*(a) **Bond Redemption Adjustment**: Reduced by $74,140,000 (subject to adjustment for accrued interest through actual redemption date) to reflect Seller's obligation to redeem all outstanding tax-exempt bonds pursuant to Section 2.3.*

*(b) **Restricted Endowment Adjustment**: Reduced by $18,400,000 to reflect Seller's retention of all permanently restricted endowment funds transferred to the Educational Foundation pursuant to Section 2.7.*

*(c) **Research Program Wind-Down Adjustment**: Reduced by $8,200,000 to reflect anticipated federal grant terminations and research program contraction costs (Section 2.8).*

*(d) **Net Purchase Price**: $779,260,000 after adjustments, payable as follows:*
- *(i) $700,570,000 in cash at Closing*
- *(ii) $38,690,000 deposited into Escrow Accounts per Section 2.5*
- *(iii) $40,000,000 in Buyer stock (4-year vesting, subject to employment continuation)*

*Total Sources of Consideration: $687,000,000 (enterprise value after adjustments)."*

**Section 2.5 - Escrow Arrangements (Multi-Tranche Structure):**

| Escrow Account | Amount | Purpose | Release Terms | Duration |
|----------------|--------|---------|---------------|----------|
| **General R&W Escrow** | $15.6M (2% of EV) | Seller breach of representations/warranties | Pro rata quarterly release over 24 months if no claims; 20% holdback if claims pending | 24 months |
| **Title IV Compliance Escrow** | $6.4M | ED sanctions, composite score degradation, provisional certification conditions | Release upon: (1) 2 consecutive clean audits, (2) composite score ≥1.5, (3) no ED sanctions | 36 months |
| **Employment Transition Escrow** | $7.15M | Tenure buyouts, WARN Act compliance, faculty retention | Draws for documented tenure transition costs; unused funds release after 18 months | 18 months |
| **Research Wind-Down Escrow** | $8.2M | Federal grant terminations, F&A rate reduction, export control compliance | Draws for documented grant loss and compliance costs; quarterly reconciliation | 24 months |
| **Accreditation Monitoring Escrow** | $1.35M | HLC sanctions, Focused Visit costs, Show Cause response | Release upon successful HLC reaffirmation without sanctions | 36 months (through next HLC cycle) |
| **TOTAL ESCROW** | **$38.7M** | **Multiple risk domains** | **Staged releases per category** | **18-36 months** |

**Escrow Draw Mechanics:**

*"(a) Buyer may draw from applicable Escrow Account upon 15-day advance written notice to Seller and Escrow Agent, providing: (i) detailed description of Loss, (ii) supporting documentation (invoices, court filings, settlement agreements, regulatory notices), and (iii) calculation showing Loss amount and relationship to escrowed risk category.*

*(b) Seller has 15 days to object to draw request. If no objection, Escrow Agent releases funds within 5 business days. If objection, dispute resolution per Section 11.7 (expedited arbitration with 30-day resolution deadline).*

*(c) Quarterly reconciliation: Within 20 days of each quarter-end, Buyer provides status report on all escrowed risk categories with updated probability assessments. Escrow Agent releases proportional amounts for categories showing reduced risk exposure.*

*(d) Final release: At escrow expiration, all unreleased funds return to Seller unless: (i) pending claims with reserves held, or (ii) Buyer has asserted indemnification claim under Section 8.2 related to escrowed category (holdback continues until claim resolution)."*

**Section 8.2 - Seller Indemnification Obligations:**

*"Seller shall indemnify, defend, and hold harmless Buyer from Losses arising from or related to:*

*(a) **Pre-Closing Regulatory Violations**: Title IV program reviews, state authorization deficiencies, accreditation sanctions based on pre-Closing conduct or conditions. **Deductible: $500K (first-dollar for ED sanctions). Cap: $15M.***

*(b) **Pre-Closing Tax Liabilities**: Federal/state/local tax assessments for periods prior to Closing, including unrelated business income tax (UBIT) audits, payroll tax deficiencies, property tax disputes. **Deductible: $250K. Cap: $8M.***

*(c) **Environmental Liabilities**: Pre-Closing contamination, hazardous materials violations, EPA/IDEM enforcement for pre-Closing conduct. **Deductible: $100K (environmental claims only). Cap: $5M.***

*(d) **Undisclosed Litigation**: Any lawsuit filed or threatened but not disclosed on Schedule 4.8 (Litigation); settlements and judgments for claims arising from pre-Closing events. **No deductible (fraud/intentional nondisclosure). Cap: $12M.***

*(e) **Student Consumer Protection Claims**: Class actions or regulatory investigations arising from pre-Closing misrepresentations, deceptive practices, or consumer protection violations. **Deductible: $500K. Cap: $10M.***

*(f) **Total Indemnification Cap: $50M** (aggregate across all categories). **Survival Period: 24 months** (36 months for tax, 18 months for R&W). Claims must be asserted before survival expiration; resolution may extend beyond."*

**Section 6.4 - Seller Interim Operating Covenants:**

*"From execution through Closing (estimated 120-180 days), Seller covenants to:*

*(a) **Maintain Title IV Eligibility**: Submit all required ED reports timely; respond to program reviews within 30 days; take no action jeopardizing provisional certification; notify Buyer within 24 hours of any ED communication.*

*(b) **Preserve Accreditation**: Respond to HLC inquiries; prepare and submit Focused Visit materials if required; avoid policy changes triggering substantive change notifications without Buyer pre-approval.*

*(c) **Stabilize Enrollment**: Maintain marketing spend at prior-year levels ($4.2M quarterly); offer admission to qualified applicants consistent with historical standards; provide accurate conversion disclosures to prospective students per Buyer-approved script.*

*(d) **Minimize Faculty Attrition**: Do not announce tenure elimination until post-Closing; offer voluntary early retirement only with Buyer pre-approval; maintain faculty compensation and benefits at current levels.*

*(e) **Preserve Research Grants**: Submit grant continuation applications timely; notify federal sponsors of pending ownership change per 2 C.F.R. § 200.308; coordinate with Buyer on grant transfer vs. termination decisions.*

*(f) **Notice of Material Changes**: Within 5 business days, notify Buyer of: (i) ED inquiries/sanctions, (ii) state authorization issues, (iii) HLC communications, (iv) enrollment declines >10% vs. prior year, (v) faculty resignations of 10+ faculty, (vi) vendor contract terminations >$250K annually, (vii) litigation filed or threatened >$500K, (viii) Title IV cohort default rate increases.*

*(g) **Obtain Required Consents**: Use commercially reasonable efforts to obtain third-party consents for contract assignments (vendor, lease, partnership agreements); estimated 47 consents required per Schedule 6.4(g)."*

**Section 7.1 - Closing Conditions (Buyer):**

*"Buyer's obligation to close is subject to satisfaction (or waiver) of:*

*(a) **Title IV Provisional Status Maintained**: ED has not terminated, suspended, or imposed additional conditions on provisional certification; no open program reviews with preliminary adverse findings.*

*(b) **State Authorization Approvals**: Indiana ICHE approval obtained; no adverse conditions imposed; authorization effective upon Closing; bonds posted for states requiring financial surety (estimated 8 states, $12.4M total).*

*(c) **HLC Substantive Change Approval**: Application submitted 90+ days pre-Closing; no Show Cause or adverse action threatened; HLC confirms continued accreditation post-conversion (may include monitoring or Focused Visit requirement - acceptable if not probation/suspension).*

*(d) **Key Contract Consents Obtained**: Written consents received for: (i) Student Information System (Ellucian), (ii) Learning Management System (Canvas), (iii) Off-Campus Housing Master Lease, (iv) Corporate Partnership Agreements (7 of 11 required). Failure to obtain consents for other contracts does not prevent Closing but reduces Purchase Price by 2× annual contract value.*

*(e) **No Material Adverse Effect**: No MAE as defined in Section 10.2 has occurred and is continuing; for clarity, the following do NOT constitute MAE: (i) general market conditions affecting nonprofit-to-for-profit education sector, (ii) enrollment declines <15%, (iii) faculty resignations <20 faculty, (iv) disclosed regulatory matters in Schedules 4.1-4.10.*

*(f) **Financing Commitment**: Buyer has obtained committed financing sufficient to: (i) pay cash consideration at Closing, (ii) redeem all tax-exempt bonds with make-whole premiums, (iii) fund escrow accounts, (iv) provide $50M working capital for first-year operations.*

*(g) **Regulatory Notifications Complete**: All required change-of-control notifications submitted to: ED (90+ days pre-Closing), state authorizers (per state requirements, 30-180 days), HLC (90+ days), NCAA (30+ days), federal grant sponsors (per 2 C.F.R. § 200.308)."*

**Section 10.2 - Material Adverse Effect Definition:**

*"'Material Adverse Effect' means any event, occurrence, fact, condition, or change that is, or would reasonably be expected to be, materially adverse to (a) the business, results of operations, condition (financial or otherwise), or assets of the University, or (b) the ability of Seller to consummate the transactions contemplated by this Agreement; **provided, however, that Material Adverse Effect shall not include any event, occurrence, fact, condition, or change, directly or indirectly, arising out of or attributable to:***

*(i) general economic conditions or conditions generally affecting nonprofit or for-profit higher education institutions in the United States;*
*(ii) changes in GAAP or regulatory accounting requirements applicable to higher education institutions;*
*(iii) changes in laws, rules, regulations, orders, or other binding directives issued by any governmental authority (including ED guidance, state authorization requirements, or accreditation standards), except to the extent such changes have a disproportionate effect on the University compared to other similarly situated institutions;*
*(iv) the announcement of this Agreement or the pendency of the transactions contemplated hereby (including any impact on enrollment, faculty retention, donor relations, or vendor relationships);*
*(v) any matter disclosed in the Disclosure Schedules, including all risks identified in Schedules 4.1 through 4.10;*
