*(vi) enrollment declines not exceeding 15% compared to the prior corresponding academic term;*
*(vii) faculty or staff resignations not exceeding 20 faculty or 35 staff;*
*(viii) failure to meet financial projections or forecasts (but not the underlying facts or circumstances causing such failure, unless independently excluded);*
*(ix) loss or termination of federal research grants categorically ineligible for for-profit institutions (as identified in Section VIII and Schedule 4.6);*
*(x) Title IV cohort default rate increases not exceeding 3 percentage points;*
*(xi) state authorization bond requirements or financial surety demands not exceeding $15M in aggregate;*

*Any such effect that is not excluded by clauses (i)-(xi) shall be considered in determining whether a Material Adverse Effect has occurred, using the standard: events that individually or in the aggregate result in (A) loss of Title IV eligibility, (B) loss of institutional accreditation, (C) enrollment decline >25%, (D) ED sanctions imposing letter of credit >$40M, or (E) litigation judgments or settlements exceeding $30M not covered by insurance."*

#### C. Recommended Purchase Price Adjustments

**Base Purchase Price (Announced Transaction):** $780,000,000

**Category 1 - Structural Adjustments (Dollar-for-Dollar Reductions):**

| Adjustment Category | Amount | Rationale | Section Reference |
|---------------------|--------|-----------|-------------------|
| Tax-exempt bond redemption | ($74,140,000) | Mandatory redemption upon 501(c)(3) loss; make-whole premiums | Section X.C |
| Restricted endowment retention | ($18,400,000) | Donor restrictions incompatible with for-profit; transfer to foundation | Section X.D |
| Research program wind-down | ($8,200,000) | NSF/NIH grant categorical ineligibility; F&A rate reduction | Section VIII.A-B |
| **Subtotal - Structural Adjustments** | **($100,740,000)** | **Enterprise value reductions** | **—** |

**Category 2 - Risk-Adjusted Operational Adjustments:**

| Adjustment Category | Probability-Weighted Exposure | Discount Rate | Present Value Adjustment | Section Reference |
|---------------------|------------------------------|---------------|-------------------------|-------------------|
| Title IV ongoing compliance costs | $3.2M annually × 5 years | 70% probability × 8% discount | ($10,750,000) | Section II.E |
| State authorization bond/surety | $12.4M (8 states) | 60% probability | ($7,440,000) | Section III.D |
| Student enrollment decline | $8.4M annually × 3 years | 85% probability × 8% discount | ($17,890,000) | Section V.C |
| Property tax exemption loss | $1.84M annually (perpetual) | 100% probability × 6% discount | ($30,667,000) | Section X.B.3 |
| NCAA Division II membership risk | $3.8M annually × 5 years | 45% probability × 8% discount | ($6,830,000) | Section VII.C |
| Faculty retention differential | $1.35M annually × 5 years | 100% probability × 8% discount | ($5,390,000) | Section IX.A.2 |
| **Subtotal - Operational Adjustments** | **—** | **Risk-adjusted present value** | **($78,967,000)** | **—** |

**Category 3 - Insurance/Mitigation Credits:**

| Credit Category | Amount | Rationale | Section Reference |
|-----------------|--------|-----------|-------------------|
| R&W insurance policy | $25,000,000 | Buyer obtains $40M policy covering unknown liabilities; $25M reduces net exposure | N/A |
| Escrow accounts (present value) | $34,200,000 | $38.7M escrowed funds discounted to present value (weighted average 24-month duration at 6% rate) | Section XI.B |
| Seller indemnifications (capped) | $18,900,000 | $50M indemnification cap discounted for: (1) 38% expected utilization rate, (2) enforcement/collection risk | Section XI.B |
| **Subtotal - Mitigation Credits** | **$78,100,000** | **Reduces Buyer net exposure** | **—** |

**Adjusted Enterprise Value Calculation:**

```
Base Purchase Price (announced):                              $780,000,000

Less: Category 1 (Structural Adjustments)                    ($100,740,000)
Less: Category 2 (Operational Adjustments)                    ($78,967,000)
Plus: Category 3 (Mitigation Credits)                         $78,100,000

Adjusted Enterprise Value:                                    $678,393,000

Net Purchase Price Reduction:                                ($101,607,000)  (13.0% reduction)
```

**Alternative Transaction Structures with Different Risk Allocations:**

**Option A - Seller-Favorable (Current Structure):**
- Purchase Price: $678.4M (13% reduction)
- Buyer bears: 61% of operational risks
- Seller bears: 39% through price reductions/escrows
- **Rationale:** Seller provides significant concessions ($101.6M) in exchange for deal certainty and limited post-closing exposure (capped indemnifications, finite escrow periods)

**Option B - Buyer-Favorable (Aggressive Risk Transfer):**
- Purchase Price: $615.0M (21% reduction)
- Buyer bears: 35% of operational risks
- Seller bears: 65% through deeper price cuts, uncapped indemnifications, longer escrows
- **Rationale:** Buyer demands maximum protection given significant regulatory uncertainties; Seller accepts lower valuation to complete transaction
- **Additional Terms:** (1) Uncapped indemnification for Title IV/accreditation (5-year survival), (2) $62M total escrows with 48-month duration, (3) Earnout structure: $50M payable if enrollment >95% baseline after 3 years

**Option C - Shared-Risk Partnership Structure:**
- Purchase Price: $725.0M (7% reduction)
- Buyer bears: 50% of operational risks (split evenly)
- Seller retains 15% equity in Buyer entity (participating preferred)
- **Rationale:** Seller maintains upside participation if operational risks don't materialize; Buyer gets higher purchase price but shares long-term risk
- **Additional Terms:** (1) Seller appoints 2 board members for 5 years, (2) Seller preferred equity redeemable after Year 5 at 2× if successful, (3) Shared governance on major decisions (accreditation, Title IV, enrollment strategy)

**Recommended Structure:** **Option A (Current Structure at $678.4M)** balances risk allocation with deal certainty. Option B creates excessive seller exposure potentially preventing deal closing. Option C introduces governance complexity undesirable for financial buyer.

#### D. Implementation Timeline and Critical Path

**Phase 1 - Pre-Signing (60-90 Days):**

| Milestone | Timeline | Responsible Party | Dependencies | Risk if Delayed |
|-----------|----------|------------------|---------------|-----------------|
| **Due diligence completion** | Weeks 1-8 | Buyer (this memo) | Access to data room, management interviews | Extends signing timeline; stale diligence |
| **Transaction agreement negotiation** | Weeks 4-10 | Both parties' counsel | Diligence findings inform reps/warranties | Misaligned risk allocation |
| **Regulatory strategy finalized** | Weeks 6-9 | Regulatory counsel + consultants | ED/HLC/state approval pathways determined | Wrong sequencing; approval delays |
| **Financing commitment obtained** | Weeks 8-12 | Buyer + lenders | Due diligence complete; lender underwriting | Deal cannot close without financing |
| **Board approvals (both parties)** | Week 10-12 | Boards of Directors/Trustees | Transaction agreement negotiated | Cannot execute definitive agreement |
| **SIGNING** | **Day 90** | **Both parties** | **All above complete** | **—** |

**Phase 2 - Post-Signing Regulatory Approvals (120-180 Days):**

**Critical Path:** The longest regulatory approval timeline governs overall closing date. Based on analysis:

**Governing Timeline: HLC Substantive Change (120-150 days)**

**Sequential Workflow:**

```
Day 0 (Signing) → Day 30: Submit applications to all agencies (parallel processing begins)

Parallel Track A - Federal (ED):
Day 0 → Day 30: Prepare ED change of ownership application
Day 30: Submit to ED Federal Student Aid (90-day advance notice satisfied)
Day 60-90: ED processing, possible questions/supplemental info requests
Day 120: ED issues approval (provisional certification continues with possible new conditions)

Parallel Track B - State Authorization:
Day 0 → Day 30: Prepare ICHE application + applications for 22 other states
Day 30: Submit to Indiana ICHE + reciprocity states
Day 45-75: State processing (varies by state: IN = 60 days, CA = 90 days, FL = 45 days)
Day 90: Majority of state approvals received
Day 105: Bond requirements determined for states demanding surety (8 states, $12.4M posted)

Parallel Track C - Accreditation (CRITICAL PATH):
Day 0 → Day 45: Prepare HLC substantive change application (comprehensive, 150+ pages)
Day 45: Submit to HLC (meets 90-day advance notice requirement)
Day 75: HLC staff review complete; assigned to Institutional Actions Council (IAC)
Day 105: IAC meeting #1 - preliminary review, possible questions
Day 120: Respond to HLC questions with supplemental materials
Day 135: IAC meeting #2 - final review and vote
Day 145-150: HLC issues formal decision (approval with monitoring vs. Focused Visit vs. denial)

Parallel Track D - Other Required Consents:
Day 0 → Day 90: Negotiate vendor consents (47 contracts requiring consent)
Day 60: Majority of non-critical consents obtained
Day 90: Critical consents obtained (SIS, LMS, housing) - remaining consents subject to price adjustment
```

**Closing Date:** **Day 150-180** (depending on HLC timeline and any supplemental information requests)

**Phase 3 - Pre-Closing Readiness (Days 120-180):**

| Milestone | Timeline | Responsible Party | Dependencies | Criticality |
|-----------|----------|------------------|---------------|-------------|
| **Taxable bond financing closed** | Day 135-145 | Buyer + bond underwriters | HLC approval near-certain; lender underwrites | **CRITICAL** - cannot close without $74.1M redemption funds |
| **Escrow accounts established** | Day 140-150 | Escrow agent (U.S. Bank) | Transaction agreement executed; escrow schedules finalized | **HIGH** - $38.7M must be deposited at Closing |
| **Educational Foundation created** | Day 100-120 | Seller + nonprofit counsel | Indiana Secretary of State filing; 501(c)(3) determination letter | **CRITICAL** - $18.4M endowment transfers at Closing |
| **Student enrollment agreements amended** | Day 150-160 | Seller (pre-Closing) | Conversion disclosure approved by Buyer and regulatory counsel | **HIGH** - students sign amended agreements within 30 days post-Closing |
| **Employee communications plan** | Day 120-140 | Both parties (joint) | Tenure transition strategy finalized; WARN Act compliance confirmed | **HIGH** - reduces faculty/staff attrition risk |
| **Vendor transition plans** | Day 100-150 | Buyer operations team | Consents obtained or price adjustments determined | **MODERATE** - alternatives identified for non-consenting vendors |
| **CLOSING** | **Day 150-180** | **Both parties** | **All regulatory approvals received** | **—** |

**Phase 4 - Post-Closing Integration (Days 180-540):**

**First 90 Days Post-Closing (Critical Stabilization Period):**

| Priority | Action Items | Owner | Success Metrics | Risk if Failed |
|----------|-------------|-------|-----------------|----------------|
| **1. Title IV Compliance** | File ownership change updates with ED; submit first for-profit financial statements; respond to any ED inquiries within 10 days | CFO + Compliance Officer | No ED sanctions; provisional status maintained | Loss of Title IV eligibility ($167M revenue) |
| **2. Student Retention** | Execute amended enrollment agreements with 95%+ of students; launch student communication campaign; offer retention incentives | Enrollment VP | <10% student attrition by end of first semester | Enrollment decline triggers ED composite score recalculation |
| **3. Faculty Transition** | Launch voluntary tenure buyout program; communicate at-will transition timeline; retain 80%+ of faculty | HR + Provost | 116+ of 145 faculty retained through first year | Teaching capacity shortage; accreditation risk |
| **4. Vendor Continuity** | Transition to replacement vendors where consents not obtained; renegotiate pricing where required | Procurement + IT | No operational disruptions to SIS, LMS, critical systems | Student services degradation; compliance failures |
| **5. State Authorization Bonds** | Post required surety bonds in 8 states; file ownership change confirmations in all 50 states | Legal + Compliance | All state authorizations active within 90 days | Cannot enroll students in non-authorized states |

**Days 90-180 Post-Closing (Operational Stabilization):**

| Priority | Action Items | Owner | Success Metrics | Risk if Failed |
|----------|-------------|-------|-----------------|----------------|
| **6. HLC Monitoring Compliance** | Submit required reports to HLC per approval conditions (likely quarterly financial reports + annual progress report) | Accreditation Liaison Officer | Reports submitted timely; no HLC sanctions | Show Cause or probation |
| **7. Research Program Wind-Down** | Coordinate grant transfers or closures with federal sponsors; transition research staff; document close-out costs for escrow draw | Research Administration | Orderly grant closures; escrow draws processed | Disallowed costs; reputational damage with sponsors |
| **8. Financial System Conversion** | Convert from nonprofit accounting (FASB ASC 958) to for-profit GAAP; establish for-profit internal controls | Controller + Auditors | Clean first-year audit opinion | ED financial responsibility issues; lender covenant violations |
| **9. NCAA Transition** | If Division II membership at risk, initiate Division III application OR transition to NAIA; stabilize athletic program | Athletic Director | Continued athletic conference membership | Loss of 18 varsity sports; student-athlete attrition |
| **10. Marketing Rebrand** | Refresh brand positioning as for-profit; address "quality concerns" in marketplace; student recruitment campaigns | Marketing + Enrollment | Applications for next year at 85%+ of baseline | Enrollment spiral accelerates |

**Days 180-365 Post-Closing (Long-Term Sustainability):**

| Priority | Action Items | Owner | Success Metrics | Risk if Failed |
|----------|-------------|-------|-----------------|----------------|
| **11. Alumni Re-Engagement** | Launch alumni campaign addressing conversion; focus on career services value proposition; stabilize giving | Advancement VP | Annual fund giving at 60%+ of pre-conversion baseline | Permanent donor loss; reputational damage |
| **12. Retention Improvement** | Implement student success initiatives; improve completion rates; demonstrate outcomes | Student Affairs + Academic Affairs | First-to-second year retention >75% (vs. 72% baseline) | Enrollment decline compounds year-over-year |
| **13. Escrow Reconciliations** | Document all costs covered by escrow draws; prepare for escrow releases at 18/24/36 month marks | Finance + Legal | Maximum escrow utilization; support all draw requests | Forfeiture of escrowed funds; out-of-pocket costs |
| **14. Faculty Compensation Competitiveness** | Assess market rate for at-will faculty in for-profit sector; adjust compensation to retain top performers | HR + Provost | Faculty turnover <15% annually (vs. 8% nonprofit baseline) | Brain drain; teaching quality decline; accreditation risk |
| **15. Continuous Compliance Monitoring** | Establish compliance dashboard tracking all key metrics (enrollment, retention, CDR, Title IV, accreditation) | Compliance Officer | Real-time visibility; early warning for regulatory risks | Blindsided by regulatory sanctions |

**Critical Path Dependencies for Transaction Success:**

```
Pre-Signing Due Diligence (90 days)
    ↓
Definitive Agreement Execution
    ↓
Regulatory Approvals (parallel, 120-180 days)
    ├─→ ED Approval (90-120 days)
    ├─→ State Authorizations (60-105 days)
    └─→ HLC Approval (120-150 days) ← **CRITICAL PATH**
    ↓
Pre-Closing Readiness (concurrent with approvals)
    ├─→ Bond Financing ($74.1M for redemption)
    ├─→ Escrow Setup ($38.7M)
    └─→ Foundation Creation ($18.4M endowment transfer)
    ↓
CLOSING (Day 150-180)
    ↓
Post-Closing Integration
    ├─→ First 90 Days: CRITICAL STABILIZATION
    ├─→ Days 90-180: Operational Stabilization
    └─→ Days 180-365: Long-Term Sustainability
    ↓
Escrow Releases (18/24/36 months)
    └─→ Year 3: HLC Reaffirmation (accreditation certainty achieved)
```

**Transaction Timeline Summary:**
- **Signing to Closing:** 150-180 days (5-6 months)
- **Closing to Stabilization:** 90-180 days (3-6 months)
- **Total Timeline to Operational Stability:** 12-15 months from signing
- **Full Regulatory Certainty:** 36 months (through HLC accreditation reaffirmation)

#### E. Overall Transaction Recommendation and Strategic Considerations

**Bottom Line Assessment:**

The $780M acquisition of [University] with conversion from nonprofit to for-profit status is **economically viable but operationally high-risk**, requiring:
1. **$101.6M purchase price reduction** (13% discount) to $678.4M adjusted enterprise value
2. **$38.7M in escrow arrangements** with 18-36 month durations covering specific risk categories
3. **$50M capped seller indemnifications** for pre-closing liabilities and compliance failures
4. **Rigorous post-closing operational excellence** to manage $36.1M in ongoing annual cost increases and market positioning challenges

**Transaction Viability Analysis:**

**✓ PROCEED** if Buyer can satisfy the following conditions:

**Financial Conditions:**
- Available capital: $750M+ (enterprise value + transaction costs + working capital reserves)
- Committed financing: $74.1M for bond redemption + $38.7M for escrows = $112.8M dedicated sources
- Risk tolerance: Ability to absorb $136.8M first-year operational risks with 69% probability of partial materialization
- IRR expectations: Modest (12-15% unlevered) given significant execution risk and 3-5 year value creation timeline

**Operational Conditions:**
- **Higher education operational expertise**: Prior experience with for-profit university operations, Title IV compliance, regional accreditation management
- **Regulatory relationship management**: Ability to work constructively with ED, HLC, state authorizers during 150-180 day approval process
- **Brand repositioning capability**: Marketing expertise to reposition institution as quality for-profit alternative in market with significant brand skepticism
- **Workforce management experience**: Ability to manage tenure elimination, faculty retention, potential unionization campaign, and benefits transition (403(b) to 401(k))

**Strategic Conditions:**
- **Portfolio fit**: Acquisition aligns with Buyer's existing higher education portfolio or provides platform for multi-university rollup strategy
- **Market positioning**: Buyer has defensible thesis for how for-profit [University] competes against nonprofit alternatives in Indiana/regional market
- **Regulatory risk appetite**: Willingness to accept 25-35% probability of ED sanctions, HLC monitoring, or state authorization restrictions during first 3 years
- **Time horizon**: Investment holds justified for 7-10+ years given value creation timeline and regulatory stabilization requirements

**✗ DO NOT PROCEED** if any of the following apply:

**Red Flags - Deal Killers:**
- Buyer lacks higher education operational experience (first foray into education sector)
- Buyer cannot obtain committed financing for $74.1M bond redemption (no refinancing alternative exists)
- Seller unwilling to accept $101.6M purchase price reduction (maintains $780M valuation despite identified risks)
- HLC provides preliminary negative feedback during pre-application consultation (indicates approval unlikely)
- ED raises significant concerns during informal discussions about ownership change (suggests opposition)
- Enrollment declines >15% between signing and closing (triggers MAE; deal termination right)
- More than 25 faculty resign during interim period (creates teaching capacity crisis; accreditation risk)
- Key vendor consents not obtained (SIS, LMS, housing) AND replacement vendors unavailable or unaffordable

**Yellow Flags - Proceed with Caution:**
- First-year enrollment projections show >20% decline (may require additional price reduction or earnout structure)
- HLC approval comes with Focused Visit requirement in Year 2 (acceptable but increases operational burden)
- More than 3 states deny authorization or impose financial surety >$20M total (limits online growth; increases capital requirements)
- Seller requests earnout structure (adds complexity; prefer clean exit)
- Due diligence uncovers additional material liabilities not contemplated in this analysis (requires updated risk assessment and price adjustment)

**Strategic Alternatives to Direct Acquisition:**

If risks are deemed too significant for outright purchase at $678.4M, Buyer should consider:

**Alternative 1 - Joint Venture Structure:**
- Seller retains 30-40% equity in converted entity
- Seller maintains responsibility for regulatory relationships during 3-year transition
- Buyer provides capital and operational expertise
- Exit via Buyer buyout of Seller equity at Year 3-5 based on performance earnout
- **Advantages:** Aligns incentives; Seller maintains "skin in game" for smooth transition; reduces upfront capital requirement
- **Disadvantages:** Governance complexity; potential conflicts on strategy; minority equity may limit Buyer control

**Alternative 2 - Management Agreement (Asset-Light):**
- Seller remains nonprofit owner of university
- Buyer provides management services (enrollment, marketing, student services, technology) via long-term agreement
- Revenue share: Buyer receives 60-70% of tuition revenue; Seller receives 30-40% to fund academics and facilities
- Buyer has operational control without ownership; avoids regulatory change-of-control approvals
- **Advantages:** Avoids Title IV, HLC, state authorization changes; preserves nonprofit tax benefits; faster implementation (no 150-180 day approval timeline)
- **Disadvantages:** Regulatory scrutiny of "bundled services" arrangements (ED concerns about "de facto" ownership); Limited Buyer upside (no equity appreciation); Seller retains ultimate control (can terminate agreement)

**Alternative 3 - Staged Acquisition (Probationary Period):**
- Initial transaction: Purchase 70% equity; Seller retains 30%
- Buyer operates for 2 years under strict performance metrics
- If metrics achieved (enrollment, Title IV compliance, accreditation maintained), Buyer exercises option to acquire remaining 30% at predetermined formula
- If metrics not achieved, Seller has option to repurchase Buyer's 70% at cost (put option)
- **Advantages:** Reduces Buyer downside risk; provides "test drive" before full commitment; Seller maintains interest in success
- **Disadvantages:** Complex governance; potential dispute over performance metrics; Seller must accept deferred liquidity

**Recommended Path Forward:**

**PROCEED WITH ACQUISITION** at adjusted purchase price of $678.4M, subject to:

**Immediate Next Steps (Pre-Signing):**
1. **HLC Informal Consultation** (Week 1-2): Engage HLC staff informally to preview substantive change application and assess likelihood of approval. If HLC expresses significant concerns, reconsider transaction or require Seller price concession.

2. **ED Title IV Pre-Application Discussion** (Week 2-3): Schedule call with ED Federal Student Aid to discuss change of ownership application, provisional certification continuation, and any expected conditions. Assess ED posture toward transaction.

3. **Vendor Consent Probability Assessment** (Week 3-4): Directly contact critical vendors (Ellucian, Instructure, housing lessor) to gauge consent likelihood. If consents appear unlikely, negotiate price adjustment in definitive agreement.

4. **Financing Commitment** (Week 4-8): Engage lenders for $750M+ financing commitment including: (i) $678.4M enterprise value, (ii) $74.1M bond redemption, (iii) $38.7M escrows, (iv) $50M working capital. Obtain commitment letter before signing definitive agreement.

5. **Definitive Agreement Negotiation** (Week 6-12): Negotiate transaction agreement incorporating all recommendations from this memorandum, including: (1) $101.6M price reduction, (2) multi-tranche escrow structure, (3) seller indemnifications with caps, (4) robust interim covenants, (5) regulatory approval closing conditions, (6) comprehensive MAE definition.

**Signing Target:** **Week 12** (90 days from commencement of pre-signing activities)

**Closing Target:** **Week 33-36** (150-180 days after signing, depending on HLC timeline)

**Post-Closing Focus:** Execute critical stabilization plan (Section XI.D, Phase 4) with intense operational focus during first 90 days to demonstrate to regulators and market that institution remains viable and committed to quality education under new ownership structure.

**Conclusion:**

This transaction is **feasible but requires sophisticated execution**. The regulatory and operational risks are substantial, but they are largely **known, quantifiable, and manageable** with appropriate transaction structuring (price adjustments, escrows, indemnifications) and post-closing operational excellence.


Buyer must bring **deep higher education expertise, regulatory relationship management skills, and patient capital** to succeed. This is not a "financial engineering" transaction or short-term flip opportunity. Value creation requires 3-5 years of operational improvements, brand repositioning, and regulatory stabilization.

The recommended **$678.4M purchase price** (13% discount from $780M) appropriately allocates risks between parties while preserving Seller's motivation to facilitate smooth transition and Buyer's opportunity for attractive risk-adjusted returns if execution succeeds.

**Final recommendation: PROCEED, subject to successful completion of pre-signing diligence activities outlined above and satisfactory resolution of any issues identified therein.**
